## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population P and time t, which is the core ODE formulation in population ecology. The relationship captures density-dependent growth, potential Allee effects, and possibly time-varying environmental conditions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (exponential growth, density-independent)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth decelerating logarithmically near carrying capacity)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with critical minimum population threshold)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with reduced per-capita rate at low density)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Richards growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (flexible asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent birth with constant death)
- Seasonal logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (logistic with periodic environmental forcing)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (generalized density-dependent growth)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial approximation of density effects)
- Time-varying Malthusian: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (linearly changing growth rate)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (logistic growth with Holling type II harvesting)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality dP_dt ~ P → exponential (Malthusian) growth regime, density-independent
- Quadratic term P*(1-cP) or P - cP² → logistic-type density dependence with a carrying capacity
- Cubic terms in P (e.g., P*(P-a)*(K-P)) → Allee effect with bistability and critical population threshold
- Logarithmic coupling P*log(K/P) → Gompertz-type growth with asymmetric approach to carrying capacity
- Sinusoidal time dependence multiplied by growth term → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing
- Fractional power P**c with 0<c<1 → sub-linear growth indicating strong cooperative effects at low density
- Ratio P/(P+c) in death/harvesting terms → saturating functional response (Holling type II)
- Difference of power laws (P**a - P**b) → competing metabolic scaling processes (anabolism vs catabolism)
- Time appearing only through periodic functions → non-autonomous system with environmental cycles
- Sign change in dP_dt at specific P values → equilibrium points; number of sign changes indicates number of stable/unstable equilibria

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
```
c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P + c6*P/(c7 + exp(-c8*(-c9 + P)))
```

With the given values:
```
0.201074*(-1 + P/5.6366)*(1 - P/10.2326)*P + 0.201074*P + 0.201074*P/(1 + exp(-5.6366*(-0.6342 + P)))
```

Let me expand the first term:
(-1 + P/5.6366)(1 - P/10.2326) = -1 + P/10.2326 + P/5.6366 - P²/(5.6366*10.2326)

So the first part is 0.201074*P*[polynomial in P] which gives a cubic + quadratic + linear terms in P.

The sigmoid term: `0.201074*P/(1 + exp(-5.6366*(-0.6342 + P)))` = `0.201074*P/(1 + exp(5.6366*0.6342)*exp(-5.6366*P))`

Let me denote α = 5.6366. The sigmoid denominator is `1 + exp(α*0.6342)*exp(-αP)` = `1 + C*exp(-αP)`.

Multiplying numerator and denominator by `exp(αP)`: `0.201074*P*exp(αP)/(exp(αP) + C)`

This can be written as `0.201074*P*exp(αP)/(exp(αP) + C)` which equals `0.201074*P*exp(P*c2)/(c1*exp(P*c2) + 1)` if we set c1 = C (a constant) and normalize.

So the GT has the structure:
- **Cubic in P** (from expanding the product)
- **Linear in P** (the c5*P term)
- **Sigmoid-weighted P term**: P/(1 + c*exp(-αP)) which can be rewritten using the form `P*exp(αP)/(c*exp(αP)+1)` or `P/(1 + c*exp(-αP))`

Now, the cubic part: 0.201074*(-P³/(5.6366*10.2326) + P²*(1/10.2326 + 1/5.6366) + P*(-1)) 

This gives terms: aP³ + bP² + dP. Combined with c5*P, we get: aP³ + bP² + (d+c5)*P.

The polynomial part (aP³ + bP² + eP) doesn't involve a sigmoid. The sigmoid part is `gP*exp(αP)/(c1*exp(αP*P)+1)`.

Now I need to find candidates that can express: **polynomial P³ + P² + P** (no sigmoid) **plus** a sigmoid term **P·exp(αP)/(c1·exp(αP)+1)**.

Looking at candidates with structure `P³/(sigmoid) + P²/(sigmoid) + P*exp/(sigmoid)`:

**Candidate 17**: `P³*c0/(c1*exp(P*c2)+1) + P³*c3*exp(P*c2)/(c1*exp(P*c2)+1) + P²*c4/(c1*exp(P*c2)+1) + P*c5/(c1*exp(P*c2)+1) + P*c6*exp(P*c2)/(c1*exp(P*c2)+1)`

Note: `c0/(sigmoid+1) + c3*exp/(sigmoid+1)` = `(c0 + c3*exp(Pc2))/(c1*exp(Pc2)+1)`. If c0=c3*c1, this becomes constant c3. So P³*c3 (pure cubic). Similarly for P² and P terms.

For candidate 17: P³*(c0+c3*exp)/(c1*exp+1) + P²*c4/(c1*exp+1) + P*(c5+c6*exp)/(c1*exp+1). Setting c0 = a*c1, c3 = a gives P³*a. Setting c4 = b*c1 gives... no, c4/(c1*exp+1) alone can't be constant. We need both c4/(sigmoid) and c4_exp*exp/(sigmoid) to make a constant.

**Candidate 2** has P³ terms (both), P² terms (both), and P*exp and P/(sigmoid). This gives P³*const + P²*const + P*exp/(sigmoid) + P/(sigmoid). The P terms combine to P*(c6*exp+c7)/(c1*exp+1). This matches the structure!

Setting c0*c1=c3 makes P³ constant. Setting c4*c1=c5 makes P² constant. Then P*(c6*exp+c7)/(c1*exp+1) provides both linear P and sigmoid P terms. This matches!

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and determine which candidates can match it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(P) = c_0(-c_1 + P/c_2)(c_3 - P/c_4) \cdot P + c_5 P + c_6 \frac{P}{c_7 + \exp(-c_8(-c_9 + P))}$$

With numerical values substituted:
$$f(P) = 0.201(-1 + P/5.637)(1 - P/10.233) \cdot P + 0.201P + 0.201\frac{P}{1 + \exp(-5.637(-0.634 + P))}$$

Let me expand the first term. Let me denote $a = 0.201$, $b = 5.637$, $d = 10.233$, $e = 0.634$.

First term: $a(-1 + P/b)(1 - P/d)P = a \cdot P \cdot (-1 + P/b - P/d + P^2/(bd))$... wait, let me be more careful:

$(-1 + P/b)(1 - P/d) = -1 + P/d + P/b - P^2/(bd)$

So the first term = $a P(-1 + P/d + P/b - P^2/(bd))$
$= a(-P + P^2/d + P^2/b - P^3/(bd))$
$= -aP + aP^2(1/b + 1/d) - aP^3/(bd)$

Adding $c_5 P = aP$: the $-aP + aP = 0$, so the polynomial part simplifies to:
$$aP^2(1/b + 1/d) - \frac{a}{bd}P^3$$

The sigmoid term: $\frac{aP}{1 + \exp(-b(-e + P))} = \frac{aP}{1 + \exp(-b(P - e))} = \frac{aP}{1 + \exp(be - bP)} = \frac{aP}{1 + \exp(be)\exp(-bP)}$

Let me rewrite: $\frac{aP}{1 + \exp(be)\exp(-bP)}$. Multiply numerator and denominator by $\exp(bP)$:
$= \frac{aP\exp(bP)}{\exp(bP) + \exp(be)}$

This doesn't simplify to a standard form easily. Let me keep it as:
$$\frac{aP}{1 + C\exp(-bP)}$$
where $C = \exp(be) = \exp(5.637 \times 0.634) = \exp(3.574)$.

So the GT is:
$$GT(P) = -\frac{a}{bd}P^3 + \frac{a(b+d)}{bd}P^2 + \frac{aP}{1 + C\exp(-bP)}$$

This is a cubic polynomial in P (with no linear or constant term) plus a sigmoid-weighted P term.

Let me write it as:
$$GT(P) = \alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{aP}{1 + C e^{-bP}}$$

where $\alpha = -a/(bd)$ and $\beta = a(b+d)/(bd)$.

Now, the sigmoid term: $\frac{aP}{1 + Ce^{-bP}}$. Multiply top and bottom by $e^{bP}$:
$$= \frac{aPe^{bP}}{e^{bP} + C}$$

Or equivalently, with $C = c_1 \cdot e^{bP}$ notation... Let me think about this differently.

The key structure of GT is:
$$\text{GT}(P) = \alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{1 + \delta \cdot e^{-\lambda P}}$$

Now I need to check which candidates can express this structure.

Let me denote $S = c_1 \exp(Pc_2) + 1$ for candidates using this denominator. Note that $1/(c_1 e^{Pc_2} + 1)$ is a sigmoid-like function. If $c_2 < 0$, then $c_1 e^{Pc_2} = c_1 e^{-|c_2|P}$, giving $1/(1 + c_1 e^{-|c_2|P})$.

The GT sigmoid term is $\frac{\gamma P}{1 + \delta e^{-\lambda P}}$. With $c_2 < 0$ (say $c_2 = -\lambda$), we get $\frac{P}{c_1 e^{-\lambda P} + 1}$, which matches.

Also, $\frac{e^{Pc_2}}{c_1 e^{Pc_2} + 1} = \frac{1}{c_1 + e^{-Pc_2}}$. With $c_2 < 0$: $\frac{e^{-\lambda P}}{c_1 e^{-\lambda P} + 1} = \frac{1}{c_1 + e^{\lambda P}}$.

So terms with $\frac{f(P)}{c_1 e^{Pc_2}+1}$ and $\frac{f(P)e^{Pc_2}}{c_1 e^{Pc_2}+1}$ represent two different "regimes" of the sigmoid.

**Key insight:** The GT has the form:
$$\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{1 + \delta e^{-\lambda P}}$$

Let me see what structure candidates need. With $D = c_1 e^{Pc_2} + 1$ and $c_2 = -\lambda < 0$:

$\frac{P^3 c_0}{D} + \frac{P^3 c_3 e^{Pc_2}}{D} = \frac{P^3(c_0 + c_3 e^{Pc_2})}{D}$

For this to equal $\alpha P^3$ (a pure polynomial), we need:
$\frac{c_0 + c_3 e^{Pc_2}}{c_1 e^{Pc_2} + 1} = \alpha$

This requires $c_0 = \alpha$ and $c_3 = \alpha c_1$, giving $\frac{\alpha(1 + c_1 e^{Pc_2})}{c_1 e^{Pc_2} + 1} = \alpha$. ✓

Similarly for $P^2$ terms: $\frac{P^2(c_4 + c_5 e^{Pc_2})}{D} = \beta P^2$ requires $c_4 = \beta, c_5 = \beta c_1$.

For the $P$ terms, we need $\frac{\gamma P}{D}$ (just the non-exponential version since the GT sigmoid has $P$ in numerator without $e^{Pc_2}$).

But wait - we could also express $\frac{\gamma P}{D}$ as $\frac{\gamma P}{D} + \frac{0 \cdot P e^{Pc_2}}{D}$.

Let me now systematically check candidates.

### Candidates with structure: $\frac{P^3(A + Be^{Pc_2})}{D} + \frac{P^2(C + Ee^{Pc_2})}{D} + \frac{P \cdot \text{terms}}{D}$

**Candidate 2:** $\frac{P^3 c_0}{D} + \frac{P^3 c_3 e^{Pc_2}}{D} + \frac{P^2 c_4}{D} + \frac{P^2 c_5 e^{Pc_2}}{D} + \frac{Pc_6 e^{Pc_2}}{D} + \frac{Pc_7}{D}$

$= \frac{P^3(c_0 + c_3 e^{Pc_2}) + P^2(c_4 + c_5 e^{Pc_2}) + P(c_7 + c_6 e^{Pc_2})}{D}$

For this to equal $\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{D}$:

$\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{D} = \frac{\alpha P^3 D + \beta P^2 D + \gamma P}{D} = \frac{\alpha P^3(c_1 e^{Pc_2}+1) + \beta P^2(c_1 e^{Pc_2}+1) + \gamma P}{D}$

$= \frac{P^3(\alpha + \alpha c_1 e^{Pc_2}) + P^2(\beta + \beta c_1 e^{Pc_2}) + P\gamma}{D}$

Comparing: $c_0 = \alpha, c_3 = \alpha c_1, c_4 = \beta, c_5 = \beta c_1, c_7 = \gamma, c_6 = 0$.

Setting $c_6 = 0$: Yes! This works. ✓

**Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 1:** Same as Candidate 2 but with an extra $\frac{Pc_8}{D}$ term. This just merges with $\frac{Pc_7}{D}$ to give $\frac{P(c_7+c_8)}{D}$. Same structure as Candidate 2.

**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 5:** $\frac{P^3 c_0}{D} + \frac{P^3 c_3 e^{Pc_2}}{D} + \frac{P^2 c_4}{D} + \frac{P^2 c_5 e^{Pc_2}}{D} + \frac{Pc_6 e^{Pc_2}}{D}$

$= \frac{P^3(c_0 + c_3 e^{Pc_2}) + P^2(c_4 + c_5 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_6 e^{Pc_2}}{D}$

For GT: need $P\gamma$ in numerator (no $e^{Pc_2}$ multiplied). Here we only have $Pc_6 e^{Pc_2}$, no standalone $P$ term. Setting $c_6 = 0$ eliminates the P sigmoid term entirely, but GT needs it. So this can only match if $\gamma = 0$, which it isn't.

Wait, let me reconsider. We need:
$c_0 + c_3 e^{Pc_2} = \alpha(1 + c_1 e^{Pc_2})$ → $c_0 = \alpha, c_3 = \alpha c_1$
$c_4 + c_5 e^{Pc_2} = \beta(1 + c_1 e^{Pc_2})$ → $c_4 = \beta, c_5 = \beta c_1$
$c_6 e^{Pc_2} = \gamma$ → impossible since $e^{Pc_2}$ is not constant.

**Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 7:** $\frac{P^3(c_0 + c_3 e^{Pc_2}) + P^2(c_4 + c_5 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_6}{D}$

Same analysis: need $Pc_6 = P\gamma$ in numerator. But we also need the $P^3$ and $P^2$ parts to produce $\alpha P^3 D + \beta P^2 D$. So:
$c_0 + c_3 e^{Pc_2} = \alpha(1 + c_1 e^{Pc_2})$ and $c_4 + c_5 e^{Pc_2} = \beta(1 + c_1 e^{Pc_2})$ and $c_6 = \gamma$.

This works! ✓

**Candidate 7 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 10:** Same as Candidate 2 plus $\frac{c_8}{D}$. The GT has no constant term. Can we set $c_8 = 0$? Yes! Then it reduces to Candidate 2.

**Candidate 10 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 17:** $\frac{P^3(c_0 + c_3 e^{Pc_2}) + P^2 c_4 + P(c_5 + c_6 e^{Pc_2})}{D}$

For GT: $P^3$ part works as before. $P^2$ part: need $c_4 + 0 \cdot e^{Pc_2} = \beta(1 + c_1 e^{Pc_2})$, which gives $c_4 = \beta$ and $\beta c_1 = 0$. Since $\beta \neq 0$ (we computed $\beta = a(b+d)/(bd) \neq 0$), we need $c_1 = 0$. But if $c_1 = 0$, then $D = 1$, and the sigmoid term $\frac{\gamma P}{D} = \gamma P$ becomes just a linear term, losing the sigmoid character. Let me check if this works.

If $c_1 = 0$: $D = 1$, so the whole expression becomes $P^3(c_0 + c_3) + P^2 c_4 + P(c_5 + c_6)$, which is a cubic polynomial. But GT has a sigmoid term, so this doesn't work.

**Candidate 17 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 50:** $\frac{P^3(c_0 + c_3 e^{Pc_2}) + P^2 c_4 + Pc_5}{D}$

Same issue as Candidate 17 for the $P^2$ term - only one $P^2$ coefficient, no $e^{Pc_2}$ multiplied $P^2$ term. Same argument: need $c_1 = 0$, which kills the sigmoid.

**Candidate 50 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 3:** $\frac{P^3 c_0}{D} + P^3 c_3 + P^2 c_4 + \frac{P^2 c_5}{D} + P^2 c_6 + Pc_7 + \frac{Pc_8}{D}$

$= P^3 c_3 + P^2(c_4 + c_6) + Pc_7 + \frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_5 + Pc_8}{D}$

GT = $\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{D}$

Matching: $c_3 = \alpha$, $c_4 + c_6 = \beta$, $c_7 = 0$, and $\frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_5 + Pc_8}{D} = \frac{\gamma P}{D}$.

This requires $c_0 = 0, c_5 = 0, c_8 = \gamma$. ✓

**Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 4:** $\frac{P^3 c_0}{D} + \frac{P^2 c_3}{D} + \frac{P^2 c_4 e^{Pc_2}}{D} + \frac{Pc_5}{D} + P^{c_6} c_7$

$= \frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_5}{D} + c_7 P^{c_6}$

For GT: We need $\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{D}$.

The $P^3$ term: $\frac{P^3 c_0}{D}$ — for this to give $\alpha P^3$, we need $\frac{c_0}{D} = \alpha$, i.e., $c_0 = \alpha D = \alpha(c_1 e^{Pc_2} + 1)$, which is P-dependent. Not possible unless $c_0 = \alpha$ and $c_1 = 0$ (killing sigmoid) or we use the $P^{c_6}$ term.

If $c_6 = 3$: $c_7 P^3$ provides the cubic. Then we need $\frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_5}{D} = \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{D}$.

$\beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{D} = \frac{\beta P^2 D + \gamma P}{D} = \frac{\beta P^2(c_1 e^{Pc_2}+1) + \gamma P}{D}$

$= \frac{\beta c_1 P^2 e^{Pc_2} + \beta P^2 + \gamma P}{D}$

Comparing: $c_0 = 0, c_3 = \beta, c_4 = \beta c_1, c_5 = \gamma, c_7 = \alpha$. ✓

**Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 6:** $\frac{P^3 c_0}{D} + \frac{P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2})}{D} + Pc_5 + \frac{Pc_6}{D} + c_8 P^{c_7}$

GT = $\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{D}$

If $c_7 = 3$: $c_8 P^3$ gives cubic. Then $\frac{P^3 c_0}{D}$ needs to combine. We need:
$\frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_6}{D} + Pc_5 + c_8 P^3 = \alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{D}$

$\frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_6}{D} = (\alpha - c_8)P^3 - Pc_5 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{D}$

Hmm, this gets complicated. Let me try $c_0 = 0$:
$\frac{P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_6}{D} + Pc_5 + c_8 P^3$

$= c_8 P^3 + \frac{P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2})}{D} + Pc_5 + \frac{Pc_6}{D}$

For $\frac{P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2})}{D} = \beta P^2$: need $c_3 = \beta, c_4 = \beta c_1$.

Then $c_8 P^3 + \beta P^2 + Pc_5 + \frac{Pc_6}{D} = \alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{D}$

Need $c_8 = \alpha$, $c_5 = 0$, $c_6 = \gamma$. ✓

**Candidate 6 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 12:** Has $\sin(c_6 t + c_7)$ term. Setting $c_5 = 0$ eliminates it. Remaining: $\frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_8}{D}$

For GT: need $\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{D}$. The $P^3$ term: $\frac{P^3 c_0}{D} = \alpha P^3$ requires $c_0 = \alpha D$, impossible. Unless we absorb differently.

$\frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_8}{D}$

For this to equal $\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{D}$:

$= \frac{\alpha P^3 D + \beta P^2 D + \gamma P}{D} = \frac{\alpha P^3(c_1 e^{Pc_2}+1) + \beta P^2(c_1 e^{Pc_2}+1) + \gamma P}{D}$

But the candidate numerator is $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_3 + P^2 c_4 e^{Pc_2} + Pc_8$. There's no $P^3 e^{Pc_2}$ term! So we need $\alpha c_1 = 0$. Since $\alpha \neq 0$, need $c_1 = 0$, killing sigmoid.

**Candidate 12 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

Now let me check candidates with different structures:

**Candidate 9:** $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + \frac{Pc_2 e^{Pc_3}}{c_4 e^{Pc_3}+1} + c_5 e^{Pc_6} + c_7(Pc_8+1)^{c_9}$

GT = $\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{1 + \delta e^{-\lambda P}}$

The sigmoid term: $\frac{Pc_2 e^{Pc_3}}{c_4 e^{Pc_3}+1}$. With $c_3 = \lambda$: $\frac{Pc_2 e^{\lambda P}}{c_4 e^{\lambda P}+1} = \frac{Pc_2}{c_4 + e^{-\lambda P}}$. 

For GT sigmoid: $\frac{\gamma P}{1 + \delta e^{-\lambda P}}$. These have different forms: $\frac{c_2}{c_4 + e^{-\lambda P}}$ vs $\frac{\gamma}{1 + \delta e^{-\lambda P}}$. Setting $c_4 = 1$ and $c_2 = \gamma/\delta$... wait, no. $\frac{c_2}{c_4 + e^{-\lambda P}} = \frac{c_2/c_4}{1 + e^{-\lambda P}/c_4}$. So with $1/c_4 = \delta$ and $c_2/c_4 = \gamma$: $\frac{\gamma}{1 + \delta e^{-\lambda P}}$. ✓

So the sigmoid part matches. Now we need $c_5 e^{Pc_6} + c_7(Pc_8+1)^{c_9} = 0$ for all P. Set $c_5 = 0$ and $c_7 = 0$. ✓

Then $c_0 = \alpha, c_1 = \beta$. ✓

Wait, but $c_3$ and $c_4$ are used for the sigmoid, and $c_0, c_1$ for the polynomial. Let me verify: $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + \frac{Pc_2 e^{Pc_3}}{c_4 e^{Pc_3}+1}$ with $c_5 = c_7 = 0$.

$\frac{Pc_2 e^{Pc_3}}{c_4 e^{Pc_3}+1}$: Let $c_3 = -\lambda$ (negative). Then $\frac{Pc_2 e^{-\lambda P}}{c_4 e^{-\lambda P}+1} = \frac{Pc_2}{c_4 + e^{\lambda P}}$. 

Hmm, for GT: $\frac{\gamma P}{1 + \delta e^{-\lambda P}}$. Let me try $c_3 = \lambda$ (positive): $\frac{Pc_2 e^{\lambda P}}{c_4 e^{\lambda P}+1}$. Divide top and bottom by $e^{\lambda P}$: $\frac{Pc_2}{c_4 + e^{-\lambda P}}$. This equals $\frac{Pc_2/c_4}{1 + e^{-\lambda P}/c_4}$. Setting $c_2/c_4 = \gamma$ and $1/c_4 = \delta$: $\frac{\gamma P}{1 + \delta e^{-\lambda P}}$. ✓

**Candidate 9 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 11:** $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + \frac{Pc_2}{c_3 e^{Pc_4}+1} + c_5 e^{Pc_6} + c_7(Pc_8+1)^{c_9}$

**Candidate 8:** $\frac{P^3 c_0}{D} + \frac{P^2 c_3}{D} + P \cdot P^{c_4} \cdot c_5 + \frac{Pc_6}{D} + P^{c_4} c_7$

Set $c_6 = 0$: same as before, no $P^3 e^{Pc_2}$ term.

**Candidate 32:** $\frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_5}{D} + Pc_6 \cos(c_7 t)$

The $\cos(c_7 t)$ term depends on $t$. GT doesn't depend on $t$. Set $c_6 = 0$. Then same as before: no $P^3 e^{Pc_2}$ term.

**Candidate 32 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 33:** $\frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_3 + Pc_6}{D} + P^2 c_4 e^{Pc_5} + \frac{Pc_7 e^{Pc_2}}{D}$

$= \frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_3 + Pc_6 + Pc_7 e^{Pc_2}}{D} + P^2 c_4 e^{Pc_5}$

The $P^2 c_4 e^{Pc_5}$ term is an exponential times polynomial. GT has no such term. Set $c_4 = 0$.

Then $\frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_3 + P(c_6 + c_7 e^{Pc_2})}{D}$. No $P^3 e^{Pc_2}$ term.

**Candidate 33 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 34:** Has $\cos(c_8 t)$ in exponent. Set $c_6 = 0$ to eliminate. Then $\frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_5}{D}$. No $P^3 e^{Pc_2}$.

**Candidate 34 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 35:** Has $\sin$ term. Set $c_6 = 0$. Same structure.

**Candidate 35 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 36:** $\frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_5}{D} + c_6 \log(c_7 e^{Pc_8} + 1)$

Set $c_6 = 0$: same issue.

**Candidate 36 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

$\frac{Pc_6}{Pc_7+1}$ is rational, not sigmoid. Set $c_6 = 0, c_4 = 0$: $\frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_3 + Pc_5}{D}$. No $P^3 e^{Pc_2}$.

**Candidate 37 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 48:** $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + P \cdot P^{c_2} c_3 + \frac{P \cdot P^{c_4} c_5}{P^{c_4}+c_6} + Pc_7 + P^{c_2} c_8$

Complex structure with power terms and rational functions. For GT: $\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{1 + \delta e^{-\lambda P}}$. The sigmoid can't be represented by rational functions of power terms.

**Candidate 48 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 49:** $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + Pc_2 + c_3 + c_4 e^{c_5/P^3} + c_6(Pc_8+1)^{c_9} + c_8/P^3$

No sigmoid term. Can't match.

**Candidate 49 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

Now let me verify the matches more carefully.

For **Candidates 1, 2, 7, 10**: These all have the form $\frac{P^3(A + Be^{Pc_2}) + P^2(C + Ee^{Pc_2}) + P \cdot \text{terms}}{D}$ where $D = c_1 e^{Pc_2} + 1$.

The GT over common denominator $D$ has numerator:
$\alpha P^3(c_1 e^{Pc_2}+1) + \beta P^2(c_1 e^{Pc_2}+1) + \gamma P$
$= \alpha P^3 + \alpha c_1 P^3 e^{Pc_2} + \beta P^2 + \beta c_1 P^2 e^{Pc_2} + \gamma P$

So we need: $P^3$ coeff = $\alpha$, $P^3 e^{Pc_2}$ coeff = $\alpha c_1$, $P^2$ coeff = $\beta$, $P^2 e^{Pc_2}$ coeff = $\beta c_1$, $P$ coeff = $\gamma$, $Pe^{Pc_2}$ coeff = 0.

**Candidate 7:** Has $P^3(c_0 + c_3 e^{Pc_2}) + P^2(c_4 + c_5 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_6$. Matches with $c_0 = \alpha, c_3 = \alpha c_1, c_4 = \beta, c_5 = \beta c_1, c_6 = \gamma$. ✓

**Candidate 2:** Same as 7 plus $Pc_6 e^{Pc_2}$. Set $c_6 = 0$. ✓

**Candidate 1:** Same as 2 plus extra $Pc_8/D$ (redundant with $Pc_7/D$). ✓

**Candidate 10:** Same as 2 plus $c_8/D$. Set $c_8 = 0$. ✓

**Candidate 3:** $P^3 c_3 + P^2(c_4+c_6) + Pc_7 + \frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_5 + Pc_8}{D}$. Set $c_0 = 0, c_5 = 0, c_7 = 0$: $P^3 c_3 + P^2(c_4+c_6) + \frac{Pc_8}{D}$. ✓

**Candidate 4:** With $c_6 = 3$: $c_7 P^3 + \frac{P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_5}{D}$ (setting $c_0 = 0$).

$\frac{P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_5}{D} = \beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{D}$?

$\beta P^2 + \frac{\gamma P}{D} = \frac{\beta P^2 D + \gamma P}{D} = \frac{\beta P^2 + \beta c_1 P^2 e^{Pc_2} + \gamma P}{D}$

So $c_3 = \beta, c_4 = \beta c_1, c_5 = \gamma$. ✓

**Candidate 6:** Set $c_0 = 0, c_5 = 0, c_7 = 3$: $c_8 P^3 + \frac{P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2}) + Pc_6}{D}$. Same as Candidate 4 analysis. ✓

**Candidate 8:** Set $c_0 = 0, c_3 = 0, c_4 = 2$: $c_5 P^3 + c_7 P^2 + \frac{Pc_6}{D}$. ✓

**Candidate 9:** Set $c_5 = 0, c_7 = 0$: $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + \frac{Pc_2 e^{Pc_3}}{c_4 e^{Pc_3}+1}$. The sigmoid matches as shown. ✓

**Candidate 11:** Set $c_5 = 0, c_7 = 0$: $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + \frac{Pc_2}{c_3 e^{Pc_4}+1}$. ✓

**Candidate 14:** Set $c_2 = 0, c_6 = 0$: $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + \frac{Pc_3}{c_4 e^{Pc_5}+1}$. ✓

Let me double-check Candidate 8 more carefully. $P \cdot P^{c_4} \cdot c_5 = c_5 P^{1+c_4}$ and $P^{c_4} c_7 = c_7 P^{c_4}$.

With $c_4 = 2$: $c_5 P^3 + c_7 P^2$. Plus $\frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_3 + Pc_6}{D}$.

Set $c_0 = 0, c_3 = 0$: $c_5 P^3 + c_7 P^2 + \frac{Pc_6}{D}$. ✓

Now let me also verify some remaining candidates I might have missed:

**Candidate 30:** $\frac{P^3 c_0 + P^2(c_3 + c_4 e^{Pc_2}) + P(c_5 + c_6 e^{Pc_2})}{D}$

For GT numerator: $\alpha P^3 + \alpha c_1 P^3 e^{Pc_2} + \beta P^2 + \beta c_1 P^2 e^{Pc_2} + \gamma P$

Candidate numerator: $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_3 + P^2 c_4 e^{Pc_2} + Pc_5 + Pc_6 e^{Pc_2}$

Missing $P^3 e^{Pc_2}$ term. Need $\alpha c_1 = 0$, so $c_1 = 0$ (since $\alpha \neq 0$). Kills sigmoid. ✗
